Shanghai County Government Plans to Draft a Labor Conscription Dredging River Plan for the 23rd Year 133

The Shanghai County Government previously received reports from various district offices stating that there are more than fifty rivers that need to be dredged this year. However, due to a lack of funding, implementation is difficult. Therefore, at the Third County Administrative Conference, it was proposed that two points be allocated from the original eight-point security tax per mu to be used as water conservancy funds. After repeated requests, it was approved yesterday to allocate 1.5 points as special funds for water conservancy. However, with many rivers and limited funds, progress is still difficult. At the second meeting of the Construction Committee the other day, the matter was raised for discussion. It was decided to allocate all the remaining funds from the construction fund to cover the costs of labor conscription for dredging rivers to facilitate implementation. The County Government has now drafted a plan for dredging rivers this year, and dredging can be gradually started and carried out in sequence thereafter. The plan is briefly described below:

Rivers to be Dredged 134

According to reports from various district offices, there are more than fifty rivers to be dredged this year, including the Yingbao River, with a total length of more than one hundred li. With the exception of the Yingbao River, for which a special report has been submitted and a temporary mu tax has been levied, and staff have been sent to survey it, the remaining rivers have a total length of about one hundred Chinese li. Although the width and length vary, the surveying, labor conscription, construction, and management are generally the same.

Construction Procedures 135

In accordance with Article 3 of the Revised Regulations for Labor Conscription for Dredging Rivers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province, the matters of labor conscription for dredging rivers within this county should be proposed and supervised by the Construction Committee of this county. All surveying, design, and budgeting should be handled by the construction personnel in charge of this county. As for labor conscription and construction, for larger projects with a volume of more than 100,000 cubic meters, a Project Office for Labor Conscription and Dredging of a Certain River may be established, which will be under the command of the County Chief and the construction personnel in charge, and be responsible for handling the matter. For smaller projects, the County Chief and the construction personnel in charge will directly command the relevant District Chiefs to handle the matter. This County also sent staff last month to conduct surveys of the rivers to be dredged this year, which are expected to be completed by the end of October. Then, drawings and tables will be made, the amount of earth and water will be calculated, and a budget for the construction of dams and water drainage will be prepared and submitted to the Construction Department for review. In mid-November, when the busy farming season has passed and the river tides have receded, construction can be started uniformly in early December in accordance with the plans and drawings, recruiting workers to build dams, cut off the flow, and drain the accumulated water. As for the matter of labor conscription and task assignment, for larger projects with a River Construction Office, the office will be responsible for handling the matter. For those without an office, the respective District Offices will be responsible for handling the matter. All matters should be completed by the end of November to avoid delaying the deadline for construction.

Construction Deadline 136

The rivers to be dredged this year will all commence construction in early December and be completed by the end of May next year, for a total of six months. Except in special circumstances, all projects must be completed within the time limit. The Provincial Government will first send staff to inspect and accept the projects separately, and then submit the cases to the Construction Department for review and acceptance.

Budget Estimate 137

The expenses for labor conscription and river dredging, in accordance with Article 11 of the Revised Regulations for Labor Conscription for Dredging Rivers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province, with the exception of the expenses for building dams and draining water, and the expenses for food rations in remote areas, which will be prepared according to the actual situation, all other expenses for surveying, equipment, and management should be limited to 20 to 50 yuan per kilometer. If a Project Office is established, the necessary expenses will be included. According to reports from various district offices, the rivers to be dredged in this county last year reached more than 100 Chinese li (approximately 60 kilometers). Calculating an average of 40 yuan per kilometer, the expenses for surveying, equipment, and management are estimated to be 2,400 yuan. Other expenses for building dams, draining water, and repairing bridges must be prepared after the survey is completed. It is currently estimated at 70 yuan per kilometer, totaling 4,200 yuan. The total expenses are 6,600 yuan. However, the water conservancy funds that can be levied in this county this year are only more than 3,000 yuan, and the remaining funds from the construction fund (excluding those with designated uses) are only more than 1,000 yuan. Even if all of them are allocated, they are only enough to dredge 40 kilometers of rivers. According to the regulations of Case No. 5 of the Revised Detailed Rules for the Implementation of Labor Conscription for Dredging Rivers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province, the length of the rivers to be dredged and cleared annually in each county should be 20 to 50 kilometers. This county has a small area and a sparse population, and the rivers to be dredged this year, according to the reports from various district offices, reach more than 60 kilometers, which exceeds the maximum limit. Therefore, in order to take into account the actual situation, it is still necessary to reduce the amount to 40 kilometers.

Shanghai-Sichuan Exchange Rate Soars 139

Reason: A Large Amount of Sichuan Silver Flows into Shanghai

Result: Suspension of Shanghai Goods Transportation to Sichuan

The exchange rate between Sichuan and Shanghai has soared. Every 1,000 Sichuan yuan is only worth 690 national currency yuan in Shanghai. Compared to the original exchange rate, Shanghai yuan has risen by about 200 yuan per 1,000 yuan. It is said that the reason is that in the past few weeks, 20 million yuan has been remitted to Shanghai from Chongqing, Wanxian, and other places. Until recently, huge sums of money have continued to be remitted, and banks have had to increase the exchange rate.

Restrictions on Further Increase 140

The Qingyou Securities Exchange, which specializes in buying and selling "Shen" shares, has been its main business. Because the Shanghai-Sichuan exchange rate has risen to 1,370 yuan to purchase 1,000 Shanghai yuan, the exchange is unable to open and has suspended trading in "Shen" shares. Yesterday, according to Chongqing telegrams received by the Sichuan community in this port, the Sichuan Provincial Government, in view of the soaring exchange rate affecting commerce and the market, has ordered that the Sichuan exchange rate must not exceed 1,310 yuan, or penalties will be imposed.

Suspension of Goods Transportation 141

Affected by the soaring exchange rate, the Sichuan community has found that purchasing and transporting goods to Sichuan has invisibly increased costs by 30%. It is also difficult to sell the goods after they arrive in Sichuan. Therefore, except for a small amount of essential goods being transported to Sichuan, the rest of the goods have been suspended. As a result, the volume of upstream cargo at the Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Minsheng, Jiejang, Sanbei, and other Sichuan River export ports has plummeted, accounting for only 20-30% compared to normal times. Fortunately, downstream cargo is still improving, which can slightly compensate for the losses.

Shanghai Cholera Prevention Report 145

749,625 People Injected in This City

The Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office issued its third announcement yesterday. The contents include: (1) The general situation of the epidemic this year, (2) The research results of Vibrio cholerae, (3) The future work outline, (4) Statistics of the number of people injected in this city this year, etc., all of which are very important. The announcement is recorded below: (1) In Shanghai, since the discovery of the third case of cholera on August 28, no further cases have been found so far. The same is true for other ports. However, suspected cases have been found in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and Qingdao. In short, cholera can be said to be almost non-existent in the whole of China this year. Before the summer, the Meteorological Research Group of this office predicted that there would be no cholera epidemic this year. Now, this prediction has been proven by facts. (2) Other common gastrointestinal diseases, with dysentery being the most common, but not more than in previous years. Since July, the number of patients received by the epidemic hospitals has gradually decreased, and has decreased even more significantly since the beginning of September. In addition to those suffering from dysentery, most of the patients who seek medical treatment suffer from typhoid fever, gastroenteritis, malaria, seasonal epidemics, and heatstroke. (3) In this city, since the small typhoon on August 8, the rainfall was 0.36 inches, and the weather changed slightly. Since September, there have been more cloudy and rainy days. The record on September 15 was significant. The temperature was 79.3, the relative humidity was 99, and the rainfall was 2.37 inches. Most of the low-lying areas in this city were almost swamps. (4) The research on aquatic vibrios (non-pathogenic) in ponds, lakes and rivers is still continuing. The results obtained are quite interesting. For example, the first type of organism is very rare in winter, and gradually increases from May to June and July, reaching its peak. The second type is not the same, it proliferates very much in July, and its proliferation extends directly to the end of December. During the cholera season, there are many first-class solitary bacteria (the blood reaction is the same as that of the positive cholera solitary bacteria). In the Huangpu River, various vibrios have been found to have a slight agglutination reaction with the Hangzhou cholera serum. The reaction caused by the bacteria obtained in July is relatively strong. (5) On September 14, this office held a meeting and decided to merge the Epidemiology Group and the Propaganda Group to take charge of the following matters: (1) Water testing, (2) Inspection (3) Climate research, (4) Diagnosis and treatment research, (5) Injection, (6) Serum research, (7) Bacteriophage research, (8) Statistics, (5) Publicity, and decided to apply for 1,600 yuan from Jing Bao Yang to implement the following two tasks: (A) Strive to implement injections for those who are most susceptible to infection, (B) Expand publicity work, (C) Send experts to Ningbo (one of the sources of cholera) and other neighboring areas to study the water samples. (6) In August and September, injections continued to be administered. The number of injections in August is listed below: 124,272 in Shanghai City, 58,669 in the Public Concession, 15,011 in the French Concession, 56 in the Lianglu Bureau, totaling 198,008 people. Adding the previous number of injections of 551,617 people, the total number of legal injections by the end of August was 749,625 people. (7) If there are no special circumstances this season, it is feared that cholera will no longer occur, and no more announcements will be issued this year. (8) The Ninth Conference of the Southeast Asian Tropical Medical Association held in Nanjing will hold a cholera roundtable meeting on October 6 to discuss the following important issues: the relationship between Vibrio cholerae and similar vibrios, with special attention to the comparison of their antibody elements, the reaction of bacteriophages, and the chemical organization, and the evidence of the existence of Vibrio cholerae serum races, and the relationship with the preparation of diagnostic serum. In addition to discussing prevention methods and new methods for bacteriophage diagnosis and treatment, the relationship between patients and carriers, the impact of weather and the seasonality of cholera will also be discussed. The results obtained will be published together with other documents from the conference.

The Municipal Government Plans to Formulate Measures to Promote Domestic Chinese Fir Wood 146

Two Standards Set at 30%

The Construction Industry Should Comply as a Whole

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously reported to the Municipal Government twice that the sales of domestic Chinese fir wood were completely encroached upon by foreign pine wood, requesting that the construction must select domestic Chinese fir wood to a certain percentage before a license can be issued, in order to maintain domestic production. Now it is learned that the Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Municipal Government yesterday, and two measures for referring to domestic Chinese fir wood have been drafted, and will be implemented from January 1 next year. The original text reads: "Both reports are fully understood. The two ministries of Internal Affairs and Industry have successively sent documents to the government for this case, and the Bureau of Public Works has been ordered to review and discuss the case separately. Now, according to the Bureau's reply, the Bureau has formulated two minimum standards for referring to domestic Chinese fir wood in light of the construction situation in this city: (1) The columns of bungalows shall be made of domestic Chinese fir wood, (2) The purlins of bungalows with spans not exceeding 3.5 meters or building roofs shall be made of domestic Chinese fir wood, but their minimum diameter shall not be less than 12 cm. If you approve of the implementation, please set the implementation date by your government, announce it to the public, and inform the Ministry of Industry for filing. At the same time, the Bureau will notify the technicians, technicians and deputy technicians, and construction companies that are engaged in business in this city to comply as a whole, otherwise the license will not be approved in order to maintain domestic production. Whether it is appropriate or not, it is appropriate to submit a document for review and follow, which is convenient for the public." Based on this, the two standards proposed in the review are feasible and should be approved. The implementation will be set from January 1, 24th year of the Republic. In addition to ordering the Bureau to forward the order for compliance and informing the two ministries of Internal Affairs and Industry, it is appropriate to issue instructions for notification, this approval.

The Rent Reduction Committee Urges to Set Rent Reduction Standards as Soon as Possible (Continued) 148

Some Corrections to the Statement of the Real Estate Association

(5) In Germany under Hitler, (Interest Slavery) must be overthrown as soon as possible, which is highly praised. In economic history, there are many examples of prohibiting interest and restricting interest. We are not fond of high-level discussions, nor do we want to understand each other. However, looking around the world's major cities, the interest rates are as high as those mentioned by the Real Estate Association (8.5% for foreign merchants and 10% for Chinese merchants). Please refer to the following table.

Official Interest Rate Table of Major Countries in the World (Battle Position%)

Country Year US UK France Germany Italy Japan

1913 Average 4.77 4.00 5.37 5.56 6.60 - -

1933 February 2.50 2.00 2.50 4.00 4.00 4.38

The table on the right shows the official interest rates of major countries in the world from 1913 to the end of February last year. The highest among them was 9.15% in Germany in 1925, when the country was in the midst of financial turmoil. The lowest was 2% in the United Kingdom in 1933. However, the actual interest rate of banks in the market was far lower than the official limit. For example, the average interest rate on the market in Germany in 1925 was only 7.62%, while the interest rate in London in 1933 was as low as 0.87%, and the interest rate in New York was even lower at 0.32%. From 1931 to 1933, the interest rate in Paris did not exceed 1.8%. Therefore, in terms of the world's financial situation, real estate and financial industries should not operate at high interest rates that are unparalleled in the world for housing that everyone needs. This should be noted. Furthermore, in terms of the interest rates of domestic industries, the maximum interest rate for farmers to purchase production materials cannot exceed 5%. This is something that everyone who is close to the countryside knows. Even in this city, households that save money and earn interest are satisfied with an annual interest rate of 5-6% if they encounter a reliable opportunity. For example, the interest rates of the Public Works Bureau's public bonds, telephone company shares, electric power company shares, and corporate bonds do not exceed 6%, and those who purchase them are amazed. This proves that investment households do not attempt to obtain excessive interest. Why does the Real Estate Association alone impose an interest rate of 8.5% or even 10% on tenants? This should be reviewed in terms of the domestic financial situation. Housing that everyone needs should not be charged a high interest rate that is not needed in the market.

I was going to return to my hometown, but when I rushed to the pier, the boat had already left. I waited for three days, starving to death, so I might as well commit suicide and leave the sea of misery. The district chief felt sorry for him and ordered him to be sent to the bureau for relief.

The Names of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Districts and Stations Will Be Changed from Next Month 161

Adding a Branch Bureau in Gaoqiao, Pudong

A Total of Eight Districts and Twenty-Two Police Stations

The change of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's districts and stations to branch bureaus is based on the resolution of the police affairs conference of the Ministry of Internal Affairs attended by Director Wen last year. Wen believes that the public security bureaus in Pingjin and other places have been renamed in order. The implementation in this city was originally scheduled for the 15th of this month, but the procedures were not completed, so the renaming was postponed to October 1. The Nanshi First District will be changed to the 16th Pu Branch Bureau, Dongjiadu Police Station, Yi Miao Police Station, and Xundao Street Police Station. The Second District will be changed to the Ximen Branch Bureau and Shenxiangge Police Station. The Pudong Third District will be changed to the Pudong Branch Bureau, Yangjing Police Station, Yangjiadu Police Station, and Tangqiao Police Station. The Zhabei Fourth District will be changed to the Xinzha Branch Bureau and Hengfeng Road Police Station, Menggu Road Police Station, and Zhenru Police Station. The Baoshan Road Fifth District will be changed to the North Station Branch Bureau, Yongxing Road Police Station, Linping Road Police Station, and Yinxianggang Police Station. The Huxi Caojiadu Sixth District will be changed to the Caojiadu Branch Bureau, Xujiahui Police Station, Pusong Police Station, and Caojing Police Station. The Jiangwan Seventh District will be changed to the City Center Branch Bureau, Yunzaobang Police Station, Wusong Police Station, and Jiangwan Police Station. A Gaoqiao Branch Bureau and Donggou Police Station will be added in Gaoqiao Town, Pudong. There are a total of eight branch bureaus and twenty-two branch police stations in the city. As for the powers, they will still be handled as previously stipulated, and there will be no changes.

The Post Office Opens Ordinary Express Mail 162

Starting from October 1

Shanghai Postal Administration issued Announcement No. 1160 yesterday, saying: "It is hereby decided to open ordinary express mail services from October 1 this year. All types of mail, except packages and insured mail, can be sent as ordinary express mail. Post offices across the country will handle it uniformly. In addition to the ordinary postage, an additional ordinary express fee of 5 points per item shall be charged. Two horizontal lines should be drawn at the upper and lower ends of the envelope, and the words (Ordinary Express) should be marked between the two horizontal lines at the top, as shown in the left figure, to identify the Chinese envelope style ordinary express style envelope letter. The procedures for sending and delivering ordinary express mail are the same as those for ordinary mail. No receipts will be issued or withdrawn. The responsibilities of the post office and the methods for senders to inquire are also the same as those for ordinary mail. The sending, distribution, and transportation should be as fast as possible. When delivering, except for bureaus without express couriers, they will be delivered by ordinary couriers. Bureaus that already have express couriers will be delivered by express couriers uniformly. Announcement is hereby made to inform everyone of this announcement.

The French Concession Plans to Equip Wireless Anti-Theft Cars 163

Machine Guns Hidden in the Car

The Implementation Period Will Not Be Far Away

Shanghai Times reported that the French Concession Police Station is now planning to purchase anti-theft cars equipped with wireless communication according to the method of the Public Concession, so that it can quickly respond to theft alarms, etc. The Public Concession has achieved good results since the implementation of this type of car. Therefore, the French Concession authorities are eager to follow suit. Currently, this matter needs to be approved by the Public Works Bureau, so it has not been officially announced. It is said that the implementation period must not be far away. It is also said that many types of cars are currently being considered, one of which is fully equipped with armor and unbreakable glass, and a hidden machine gun. Most of the French Concession authorities advocate adopting patrol cars equipped with wireless communication that are common in many parts of the United States. If adopted, a new type of anti-theft car will appear in Shanghai.

Wu Yongmei Died Tragically in Southeast Medical College

Hua Shuxian and Ouyang Shu's Injuries Are Also Serious

丨Culprit Lan Fuming Was Arrested丨

Lan Fuming, a student of Jinan University in Zhenru, from Guangdong, was learning to drive a car with many classmates near the Jiaotong Road beside the school at about 10 am yesterday. Although he had a little knowledge of the basics, his skills were not very good. Therefore, he was slanting from east to west along the way, and the direction was uncertain. At the same time, the speed was also suddenly slow and suddenly fast, and there was no way to grasp it. In the blink of an eye, Lan suddenly saw three female classmates walking leisurely in front of the car, and they were about to be hit. He panicked and was about to brake, but he lost his footing, causing the car to knock down all three female students who were walking in front, Hua Shuxian, Wu Yongmei, and Ouyang Shu. The wheels rubbed against their heads. Wu Yongmei was the most seriously injured. Her skull was crushed by the wheels, and blood was flowing. Ouyang Shu and Hua Shuxian were also seriously injured. Other classmates saw the serious disaster, so they screamed. At the same time, the police from the 3rd sub-station of the 4th district also rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm. They first detained the culprit Lan Fuming, and at the same time, they tried to carry the three female students Wu, Hua, and Ouyang to the Southeast Medical College near Yangjia Bridge beside the school for treatment. Wu Yongmei died at about 12 noon due to her serious injuries. Hua Shuguang and Ouyang Shu were also seriously injured and their lives were in danger. Lan Fuming is currently temporarily detained at the 3rd sub-station of the 4th district to be questioned before being handed over to the General Bureau for trial. Wu's body was inspected by the court and then sent to the funeral home by the school's friends and students, and urged Wu's family in Jiangxi to come to Shanghai to handle everything.

Carpenter, Angered by Wife's Flight, Stabs Neighbor Woman, Auntie Lu, to Death 165

Huang Xiuying's Dislike of Her Ugly Husband Was the Real Culprit

Auntie Lu's Major Intervention Leads to a Wrongful Death

丨The Culprit Fled After Committing the Crime and Remains at Large丨

Zhang Gengtao, also known as A'gen, a local carpenter, thirty-seven years old, through the matchmaking of his friend Tao Boliang, engaged Huang Xiuying (seventeen years old this year), the daughter of Huang Yinquan, a local resident of No. 139, Xiao Jiu Hua Street, outside Xiaonanmen in the southern part of the city, as his wife on the fourth day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar. He married her on the fifth day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year. After marriage, they lived together in a small room at No. 374, Block C, Rue Massenet in the French Concession. Zhang went out to work every day, leaving early and returning late, leaving Xiuying alone at home. With nothing to do in her spare time, Xiuying often went to the home of Lu Guanglin (thirty-two years old, a Ningbo native, working as a coppersmith at the Southeast Steel Factory at Xinqiao Intersection on Xietu Road), at No. 374, Block D, next door, to play. She became close friends with Lu's wife, Zhang, nineteen years old this year, who was known as Auntie Lu. After Huang Xiuying's marriage, the couple's relationship was quite affectionate, but over time, feeling that her husband was old and ugly, she felt like a bright phoenix unwilling to follow a crow. On the twenty-third day of the sixth month of the lunar calendar, she secretly ran away from her husband without a trace, secretly writing a letter to her parents, Huang Yinquan and Huang Dai, stating that she did not want to live with Zhang and asking her parents to compensate Zhang for his losses so he could marry someone else. She also said that if they wanted to know her whereabouts, they could ask Auntie Lu next door. After receiving the letter, the Huang couple went to Auntie Lu's place with Zhang to inquire. Lu Zhang said she knew nothing about Zhang's wife's escape and answered truthfully, but Zhang was not convinced. He used the letter as evidence and reported to the French police, accusing Auntie Lu of hiding his wife. The police sent detectives to investigate, but found no evidence and did not prosecute, only ordering Auntie Lu to help find her, with a deadline of three days. After the deadline, Zhang hired a lawyer to file a criminal complaint in the Special District Court, accusing Auntie Lu of disrupting the family and requesting an investigation, as well as filing a civil suit, requesting the return of his wife. Judge Li Changnian opened a court hearing on the ninth of this month to investigate the situation, which was recorded in the newspapers on the tenth. Subsequently, the court ruled that there was no evidence and declared Auntie Lu not guilty on the twelfth. At this point, Auntie Lu and her husband, Lu Guanglin, felt aggrieved by the groundless accusation in court, which damaged their reputation. They arranged to meet Zhang at the Quan'an Teahouse at the southern end of the Ba Xian Qiao Small Vegetable Market on the fourteenth to discuss compensation for the damage to their reputation. Unexpectedly, Zhang failed to appear on time, causing Auntie Lu and the people she had invited to the scene to leave disappointed. From then on, Zhang was not seen returning home. For many days, until yesterday morning, Auntie Lu learned that Zhang Gengtao was at home and went alone to Zhang Gengtao's place at nine o'clock to question him about why he had failed to appear at the teahouse on the fourteenth and to demand compensation for her reputation. The two began to argue. Zhang, feeling that his wife had been enticed to run away, and despite having his wife's letter as proof, his accusation had failed and he was now being constantly harassed, in a moment of anger, took a sharp knife and stabbed Auntie Lu three times in the right breast, chest, abdomen, navel, and left side. Lu fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. Zhang abandoned the murder weapon and fled. Lu cried out for help. The second landlord downstairs heard the commotion and went upstairs to check, finding Auntie Lu rolling in a pool of blood, blood gushing from her wounds. He was greatly shocked, and Zhang Gengtao had already fled. He reported to the French police, who sent the injured person to Guangci Hospital. Due to the severity of the injuries, the treatment was ineffective, and she died at 12:15 pm. The hospital notified the police, who sent detectives to carry the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Mortuary for an autopsy, pending a report to the Special District Court today to send someone to examine the body. The police ordered all detectives to strictly arrest the fleeing suspect and bring him to justice for questioning.

Dispute over Property Leads to Accidental Killing of Woman; Autopsy Performed 168

Police Lawyer Sues Wu Xihou

Accused of Trying to Kill His Uncle but Accidentally Killing His Wife

Wu Xihou (also known as Wu Zhangsheng), a local resident of No. 36, Maqi Road (i.e., Yida Jiao) in western Shanghai, is forty-one years old. He used to work for the British-American Tobacco Company but resigned in recent years and became a land broker, which provides him with a comfortable life. His family inherited a lot of property, and several acres of land near his residence are still co-owned with his uncle Wu Gengsheng and cousins Gengfu, Yinggui, Fusheng, and Alin. Recently, Gengsheng and others repeatedly proposed surveying the land, but Xihou opposed it each time. At 10:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, Gengsheng and others invited a surveyor from the Land Bureau, as well as the land guarantor Wang Zhenxiang and his assistant Jin Xiangsheng, to jointly survey the land. Xihou still firmly obstructed them, leading to arguments and then a major conflict between uncles and cousins. Xihou was outnumbered and suffered injuries to his head and arms. He fled home with his injuries, and Gengsheng and others followed him into his house, acting aggressively. Xihou took out a pistol for self-defense and fired into the air, hoping to scare Gengsheng and others away. At that moment, Xihou's wife, Wu Wang, fearing disaster, stepped forward to dissuade him. During the commotion, another shot was fired, hitting her in the chest. She immediately fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. The police officer from a nearby station heard the alarm and rushed to his house to investigate the cause of the incident and examine the injured woman, who had already died. The police officer reported this to the Gordon Road Police Station, which sent Deputy Inspector Moore, Officer Liu Chun, and Officer Pi Shengchang to arrest Wu Xihou and Wu Gengsheng, Gengfu, Yinggui, Fusheng, Alin, and witness Jin Xiangsheng, who had participated in the dispute. After questioning them, they detained Xihou and released the others. The body of Wu Wang was taken by the detectives to the mortuary on Filon Road. Yesterday morning, the police filed a public lawsuit against Wu Xihou, stating that he had used his self-defense pistol to shoot at his uncle Wu Gengsheng, but Gengsheng had hid behind Wu Wang, causing her to be accidentally shot and killed. Judge Yan Liangce of the First Special District Court opened a court hearing to summon the murderer and key witnesses, including Wu Gengsheng, to the court for questioning. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin explained the case and requested a postponement of the trial as the body still needed to be examined. Judge Yan questioned each witness and the defendant about the incident and then adjourned the trial to a later date. The Chinese and Western detectives in charge of the case escorted the defendant to the mortuary. Soon after, Prosecutor Tang, along with forensic doctors and court clerks, arrived at the mortuary to examine the body. They confirmed that the bullet had entered from the front of the chest but had not exited. The bullet was still inside the deceased's abdomen. Then, they began the interrogation, with the detectives first reporting the incident and the results of the investigation. Next, the defendant Wu Xihou testified that he had fired into the air to scare Gengsheng and others away, but they had not retreated, and Alin had hugged his waist tightly while Fusheng had firmly gripped the hand holding the gun, causing the gun to fire accidentally and injure his wife. However, since she had died tragically, he asked to be exempted from the autopsy and requested permission to view the remains in the morgue. Prosecutor Tang then ordered the victim's aunt, Wu Sheng, to sign a statement to claim the body for burial. As for Wu Xihou's criminal liability, the police have filed a public lawsuit and he should be detained for questioning.

Resentment of Ren Protecting the Servant

Angered, She Commits Suicide by Hanging

Ren Zhaoshi, a native of Henan, thirty-eight years old, previously held important military and political positions in Guangdong and other places. Later, he came to Shanghai and became a real estate businessman. After several years of operation, he accumulated considerable wealth. He currently lives at No. 5, Lane 516, Yuyuan Road in western Shanghai. He has a wife and a concubine living together in peace. He owns a private car and employs several male and female servants. His concubine, Gan Yulan, twenty-nine years old, is a Cantonese woman with beautiful features and is favored by Ren. She is also in charge of most of the household affairs. Unexpectedly, at around 10 a.m. on the seventeenth of this month, Ren planned to go out on business and ordered the male servant Zhu Youshan (also from Henan) to call his private car. However, the garage was several dozen paces away from Ren's house. At that time, it was raining heavily, so Zhu asked the maid to borrow an umbrella from Ren's concubine to protect himself from the rain. Unexpectedly, she refused. Zhu had to go in the rain, and he felt resentful. He muttered to himself in the kitchen. Ren's concubine happened to be there and heard him, thinking that Zhu was insulting her. She began to scold him loudly. Since the two were not from the same hometown, their language was confusing. Ren's concubine went upstairs to complain to her husband. Ren, who was in the bathroom at the time, heard both sides. Since Zhu had not said anything malicious, Ren did not blame Zhu after hearing his concubine's complaint. Instead, he rationally explained the situation to her and scolded her for not giving him the umbrella. Ren and others thought that her behavior was common and did not think much of it. Unexpectedly, the next day, she suddenly had a suicidal thought and hanged herself in the bedroom when no one was watching. When she was discovered, her face was pale and she could not speak. The detectives then carried the body to the mortuary on Filon Road. They questioned Ren Zhaoshi, Zhu Youshan, and others about the incident. Tang then ordered that the deceased, Gan Yulan, a female, had indeed died by hanging herself before death. The body was handed over to the deceased's family member, Ren Zhaoshi, who signed a statement to claim it for burial.

Doctor Hu Qipeng stated that he had treated Liu Agui after his fall. At first, he was still conscious, but he was injured in the back of the head. He said that if there was no change in forty-eight hours, there would be no problem. Later, on the second day, his condition worsened, he became unconscious, and he lost control of his bowels and bladder. He reported this to the warden, who sent him to the hospital. The official then questioned guards Nie and Chuan. The official said to inmate Zhang, "The forensic doctor has confirmed that there are no injuries on your body. What else do you have to say?" Zhang replied, "Whether I have injuries or not is not the point. Liu Agui was seriously injured at the time, and the doctor should have reported that he was injured and could not be subjected to torture. He was locked in a dark room for two days and should have been treated after his injuries healed before being dealt with." At this point, the official ordered the two inmates to be sent back to prison to await trial, and the others were dismissed. The two inmates refused to return to prison, wishing to be sent to another prison. They were eventually taken away by the bailiffs and sent back to prison.

Two Railway Bureaus Independently Trial-Produce Two Kinds of Consumables 173

Locomotive Oil... Could Save $38,000 Per Year

Storage Batteries... Could Save $25,000 Per Year

According to the Central News Agency, the two railways use over 70,000 gallons of locomotive oil per year. In 1932, Asiatic Petroleum Company (Shell) A-grade oil was purchased, which was considered the most suitable, but its price of $1.80 per gallon was uneconomical (this year's asking price has dropped to $1.35). Last year, Mobil M-brand pure mineral oil was purchased at $1.18 per gallon. Although the price was cheaper, its quality was not suitable. Only after blending in vegetable oil could it be used with difficulty. This year, the locomotive oil ordered by the railway is sold by Shengyuan Company, totaling 77,000 gallons at $0.88 per gallon, but this oil cannot be used directly in the summer. The Chemical Testing Institute, at the Wusong Materials Factory, opened a room, hired workers, and blended it with axle oil, using summer axle oil for summer use and adding a small amount of vegetable oil. The result was quite good, and the users were satisfied. After winter, they will switch to blending it with winter axle oil and still add a small amount of vegetable oil. The price of axle oil is $0.66 per gallon, so the average price of locomotive oil after blending is $0.77 per gallon, which is $0.11 less than the original price of the unsuitable Shengyuan oil. Considering the full 77,000 gallons, a total of $8,470 can be saved. Compared with last year's Mobil M-brand oil, which cost $1.28 per gallon after blending in vegetable oil, about $0.50 per gallon can be saved, for a total savings of over $38,000. In addition, for the Shanghai-Nanjing line, the passenger car storage batteries require an average of 18 to 20 new batteries per year (each car has two sets, each set containing twelve batteries). The storage batteries for long-distance telephones are not included in this figure, so the number is quite large. In the past, these were purchased from foreign countries, which was very expensive. The Shanghai Power Plant of the railway has started to manufacture its own batteries using existing equipment and labor. It has already made enough storage batteries for four cars and is currently designing new models to improve the products. The wooden boxes for the storage batteries were also ordered from foreign countries in the past. In fact, the manufacturing process is very simple, so the factory has also decided to manufacture them themselves and has started work. According to the current market price, one set of 17-brand storage batteries (consisting of 24 batteries, enough for one car) costs $1,800. The material cost of manufacturing two sets themselves is about $500. Considering the total of 36 to 40 sets per year, approximately $25,000 can be saved.

The Tobacco and Exchange Guild Writes to the Chamber of Commerce to Ask the Authorities for Compassion Regarding the License Tax 174

The Tobacco and Exchange Guild of this city has repeatedly received reports from its members that the Finance Bureau's Municipal South Collection Office has ordered the police to urge members to obtain tobacco and alcohol licenses and to pay the back taxes for the change in grade. Since the review on the city's side has not been completed, the urging to obtain licenses is considered inappropriate, and the guild has requested that the City Chamber of Commerce forward a request to the authorities for compassion. Based on this, the guild sent another letter to the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday, which reads: "Dear Sirs, upon investigation, we received a letter dated the 14th of this month, which states (omitted) that the City Finance Bureau's letter regarding the East District's members' request to reduce the tobacco and alcohol license tax has been approved, and the names of the households listed in the Pudong roster have not been raised in grade, and the licenses have been filled out and are awaiting collection. We are now returning the original receipts with a letter attached, asking each shop to collect them from that office. In addition, on the 18th, we received a letter from your esteemed association stating that Yonghe and Rongxing Hongji in Xujiahui in the West District are considered to have very prosperous cigarette businesses, and ordering them to obtain retail licenses of both grades is very fair. After investigation, the business of these shops is equivalent to that of the households in Pudong, and it is still appropriate to exchange the original licenses according to the original licenses. Those who have requested exemption from the increase are only two households, and they should be allowed to fill out licenses of the same grade to show tolerance and avoid disputes. We have now received reports from members in the South District, such as Yu Tai Xiehe Feng and other shops, that the Municipal South Collection Office has sent the police to the shops, forcing them to go to the bureau. Our shops did not dare to disobey and immediately sent clerks to the collection office with the police. They said, 'Why haven't you paid for the licenses? You must come to collect the licenses within one week, or you will be sent to the Public Security Bureau for punishment.' After investigation, our shops have all applied for tax payment and registration in accordance with the regulations. However, the receipts from our shops have been sent to your esteemed association, requesting that the City Chamber of Commerce forward a request to the Finance Bureau to exempt them from the increase. The South District has not yet received a reply from the bureau, and the office has suddenly sent the police to collect the taxes, which seems inappropriate because merchants are not given consideration. We respectfully request that the City Chamber of Commerce make a statement and request the authorities to consider the merchants' difficulties and not send the police to collect the taxes. After the City Chamber of Commerce forwards the letter to our guild, it will be convenient to collect the licenses uniformly. This would be a great favor to us. Upon investigation, the above-mentioned matters are true. We are writing to inform you of the situation and request that your esteemed association approve our request and quickly forward it to the Finance Bureau for special consideration."

The Most Complete Chinese-Run Livestock and Dairy Company 175

Substantial Capital...Comprehensive Facilities

Scientific and Hygienic...Good Quality and Low Price

The Shanghai Livestock and Dairy Company, managed by Mr. Ma Ying-piu, the general supervisor of Sincere Company, has been in operation for over a decade and has achieved remarkable results. The company advocates that to regain concessions, it is necessary to first gain the trust of the Chinese people. Therefore, it has invested hundreds of thousands of dollars to establish the most modern and complete cow sheds in Jiangwan and Wusong, paying close attention to the health of the cattle. It has long been granted an "A" grade license by the Shanghai Municipal Council. According to the latest inspection results, none of the cows at the company's Wusong branch farm have tuberculosis, setting a new record in this city. Recently, they hired the renowned Canadian veterinarian Mr. Phillips as the director of the production department, personally supervising the cattle and all aspects of hygiene. The milk produced is disinfected using the latest Pasteurizing machines. Milk processed by this machine can be drunk cold without the need for further boiling, which reduces nutritional content.

To gain the trust of the Chinese people, in addition to focusing on hygiene, the quality of the milk is also carefully considered. Most of the company's cows are purchased from the United States, and a large portion are Guernsey breeds. Therefore, the company's milk is particularly rich, with an average butterfat content of 4.6%, which is 31% higher than the health bureau's standard. The local Chinese population quickly recognized the company's reliability, and the number of customers has increased to over 3,000 households, demonstrating the high regard it enjoys in the community.

In recent years, business has been exceptionally prosperous. Last year, a pasture was added in Wusong, covering more than 600 acres, and 100 dairy cows were purchased. Recently, another 65 cows have been added and are being transported in succession. Some of these cows are worth as much as three to four thousand dollars each. There are also plans to expand the land by 2,000 acres for livestock and planting. Based on the quality of the milk produced by the company, the selling price should be higher than others. However, due to mass production to reduce costs, it is actually cheaper than other companies.

Recently, a new preferential program for long-term customers has been introduced. Customers only need to pay a small deposit of 20 yuan to enjoy an 80% discount on milk (the actual price per pound is 32 cents). This program will surely be welcomed by the community.

Shanghai Bar Association Requests Special Pardon for Qian Shao-feng 178

Student's Crime is Filial Piety and Commendable

Lu Zheng Ji-cheng's Case is a Precedent

Student Qian Shao-feng (Pei-gao), a native of An'nan County, Guizhou, is 22 years old and resides at No. 13 Yuanchang Lane, Hualong Road, French Concession, Shanghai. He is a student at a certain middle school. On the afternoon of October 16th of last year, at approximately 7:00 PM, he killed He Zun-fu, the former county magistrate of An'nan County, Guizhou, who was the murderer of his father, with a knife in the Golden Grand Theater. He was then arrested by the French police authorities and handed over to the Second Special District Local Court for prosecution and sentenced to seven years in prison. Qian Shu-sheng, the defense lawyer for Qian Shao-feng, reviewed the case file and found that Qian Shao-feng confessed that his father, Qian Bing, also known as Bin, had served as the director of the Finance Bureau of An'nan County. Due to a dispute with He Zun-fu, the county magistrate, in March of the 20th year of the Republic of China, he colluded with the local garrison and, under a pretext, had Qian Bing shot and killed. Shao-feng fled to Shanghai to study. On the evening of October 16th of last year, he passed by the Golden Grand Theater and saw He Zun-fu entering the theater to watch a movie. He immediately went back to retrieve a knife and sought revenge for his father, killing him. It is understood that seeking revenge for one's father is purely filial piety and commendable. The details of this case have been carefully written in a memorandum and a proposal has been submitted, requesting the Shanghai Bar Association to forward it to the Executive Yuan of the National Government for approval to grant a special pardon and release Qian Shao-feng from prison. It is said that the Shanghai Bar Association has submitted a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees. It was found that in Shandong Province, there was a case of Zheng Ji-cheng, who was also granted a special pardon for killing Zhang Zongchang to avenge his father. This case is similar to Zheng's case, and considering the student's commendable filial piety, a document has already been prepared and submitted to the Executive Yuan of the National Government, requesting that a special pardon be issued to save the decaying customs.

A Beef Shop on Xinmin Road Suffers from a Fire 182

Eight Buildings Were Destroyed by Fire

Shop Assistants Brought in for Questioning

At 8:20 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out in the Jiuyunxuan beef shop opened by Cao Zilong at No. 520 Xinmin Road, Zhabei, due to oil refining. In an instant, the fire raged out of control. The patrol police from the First Precinct of the Fourth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately notified the Zhabei fire brigades, who quickly dispatched fire engines to the scene. The fire had already broken through the roof. Firefighters worked hard to extinguish the fire, and it was extinguished in about two hours. A total of eight buildings were destroyed. The scene was very chaotic at the time. Director Niu Jingjian personally led patrol officers, police chiefs, and police officers to the scene to suppress the situation and maintain order, and to investigate the cause of the fire. The shop owner, Cao Zilong, fled the scene out of fear of punishment. The shop assistant Zhu Zaiqi was brought in for questioning, and a report was filed with the headquarters.

Reading Q&A

Attitude Towards Occupation (Continued) (Continued) 192

——Answer to Mr. Yuan Qingyan

The above has roughly discussed the attitude towards occupation, but at the same time, one cannot but pay attention to the attitude towards people and the attitude towards colleagues. Otherwise, you still cannot correctly deal with your occupation. - Editor

The second is the attitude towards people. People are always social beings. Society is determined by the stage of economic development at that time. Some people are progressive, and some are conservative. A person who has a good understanding of society is of course worthy of admiration, but there is no need to show any aversion to a person who is muddleheaded or glib. Because this is not only a question of their personal virtue, but the whole thing is caused by the environment. We ourselves are sober, not only should we not despise them, but we should also reflect on ourselves. Before we were sober, weren't we just as confused? We and they are only a hundred steps and fifty steps apart. What is there to be arrogant about? You should take the attitude of Mr. Sun Yat-sen. You are the first to know, and you must awaken those who know later. You have to find a way to awaken them, persuade them, and help create the conditions for them to become sober. You shouldn't let them sleep all the time. This is the correct attitude. If you can't do this, you are already wrong. If you are the only one who is awake, even if you have great abilities, what can you accomplish? You have lofty ideals, you look down on A, and you look down on B. You are indifferent to the people around you, as if they are all hostile to you. You even hate everyone around you. Oh my god, what is the use of those lofty ideals? It cannot grow in the ground, it can only exist in your imagination. What a serious mistake this is! Isn't this clearly departing from reality? Reality is ugly, the present society has diseases, and everyone is now at a dead end. The individual's way out must be based on everyone's way out, so we must all be sober and work together to reform. Now you want everyone in the world to be just like you. If you are not satisfied, you leave them. Isn't this kind of behavior the same as those who live in a drunken dream? And can you really leave them? You can't. There are impure people not only in your rice shop, but everywhere is the same. You hate them, and at the same time you will have to hate everyone in society, you will have to become the protagonist of "Diary of a Madman" (written by Lu Xun). If you really want to leave them, you must also leave life, this is unavoidable! Even if you become a monk, perhaps the monk in your ideal is higher than the monk in reality, and you will have to escape again.

Special Article

My Questions Regarding Governor Clementi's Speech at the British Malaya Association (Third Continuation) Zhou Qigang 193

(4) The Impact of Clementi's Policy

Although Mr. Clementi is British, he has lived in the East for a long time and has served as the Governor of Hong Kong. He also has studied Chinese language and literature. It was originally very appropriate for the British government to entrust him with the important task of Malaya. In theory, Mr. Clementi should have a deep understanding of China and the Chinese people. However, we associate Mr. Clementi's ban on the Chinese Kuomintang in Malaya with the 1925 (Guangdong-Hong Kong strike) storm. We feel that Mr. Clementi's policies often have unfortunate effects. British government facilities have always had a reputation for being intelligent and steady. Unfortunately, such clumsy and dangerous policies were discovered by Mr. Clementi. This cannot but make people recall the past. That storm occurred just when the Chinese Kuomintang was in power in Guangzhou. It is also possible that Mr. Clementi had some resentment about the past. The relationship between cause and effect is thought-provoking. But we should know that human beings and all living things in the world have the right to exist. Under the situation of common survival, there is only mutual assistance and mutual dependence. If a single kind of powerful force suppresses everything, then the feeling of injustice cannot be vented. Small things will lead to storms, and large things will lead to collapse. This is the first point of our concern about the impact of Mr. Clementi's policy. Since there are many overseas Chinese, the knowledge is uneven. In the past, the overseas Chinese community was divided into different categories, and there were often disputes. Since the establishment of the Kuomintang, it has often been able to come forward to mediate and dissuade these disputes. Historical facts are obvious, and people in Malaya all know this. The existence of the Kuomintang has an impact on the overseas Chinese community, and before the Chinese Kuomintang in Malaya was banned, the belief in the Three People's Principles was established in the minds of overseas Chinese, so that communism and other dangerous ideas could not invade. The actions of Kuomintang members are open and aboveboard, and can be seen at a glance. For more than ten years, they have never caused difficulties for the resident government overseas. Since Mr. Clementi banned the activities of the Kuomintang, the Communist Party has taken the opportunity to become active, secretly inciting and infiltrating everywhere. Recently, the forces of communism are said to have spread to the mines and farms of Malaya. It is difficult for the colonial government to distinguish between the Kuomintang and the Communist Party members, and the danger is difficult to prevent. This is the second point of our concern about the impact of Mr. Clementi's policy.

(5) Conclusion

To sum up, the Chinese Kuomintang has its own history of evolution overseas, especially in Malaya. Mr. Clementi's understanding of the situation of the Chinese Kuomintang in Malaya is insufficient, so the means he took are indeed regrettable. Whether the later governors will continue to implement the policies of open-mindedness, sincerity, and good neighborliness of the past British government and previous governors is also worthy of our attention. Now I hope that the overseas Chinese and Kuomintang members will, based on the spirit of coexistence and co-prosperity that has always been followed, work harder in Malaya to protect the local government and work with the local people to maintain prosperity. This is also the sympathy of the British government and Chinese and British people.

Free Talk

Cultural Backwardness and Overproduction in the Publishing Industry 194

— Yin Ming

Just as China is an economically backward country that also experiences overproduction, China is a culturally backward country that also experiences overproduction in the publishing industry. We used to see signs and advertisements for big spring sales and big autumn sales at large companies and stores, and now it's the publishing industry's turn. Look, isn't almost the entire Shanghai publishing industry, including Commercial Press, Zhonghua Book Company, World Book Company, Kaiming Bookstore, Beixin Bookstore, etc., holding big clearance sales and auctions? Moreover, they are entrusting the post office to purchase books and magazines on their behalf, banks are offering free remittances, and all kinds of sales methods are being used. Isn't this a phenomenon unique to a period of overproduction?

Is there really overproduction in the publishing industry that exceeds the needs of the Chinese people? I'm afraid no one can say that! In reality, apart from textbooks, among general publications, even very popular books that are suitable for the masses, very few can print tens of thousands of copies per edition and sell several editions a year. As for more profound theoretical readings, each edition is only printed in one to two thousand copies, and it often takes three or four years to sell one edition. With a population of 400 million and a 5,000-year cultural history, can we say there is overproduction when China only absorbs such a small amount of intellectual products?

Take our eastern neighbor as an example. With a population of only 60 million, it is very common for publications to sell tens or hundreds of editions in a few years. No wonder we are invaded by others. Just from this point of view, we are far behind.

What is the reason for this contradictory phenomenon of backwardness (which can also be said to be insufficiency) and overproduction? In my observation, like economic backwardness and overproduction, the main reasons are nothing more than the following two: (1) Cultural backwardness itself. The general cultural backwardness means that there are very few people with the ability to read, and almost the entire country is illiterate, resulting in a very low capacity to absorb intellectual products. Even within the small number of publications, overproduction is inevitable. (2) The impact of the economic panic. Most of those who can read and buy books are petty-bourgeois intellectuals. In recent years, affected by the economic panic in our country and the world, rural and urban middle and small classes have gone bankrupt, and intellectuals have lost their schooling and jobs, struggling to make a living. How can they have the spare money to buy books? How can publications not feel overproduction?

Originally, cultural products are the commodities of intellectuals (of course, there is also a layer of exploitation by booksellers in between; intellectuals are to booksellers as workers are to capitalists). Stagnant sales of commodities will affect factory closures and worker unemployment, and cultural workers are certainly no exception.

Under these circumstances, the first refuge for intellectuals is the education sector, but the education sector has long declared bankruptcy. The last and more difficult refuge is the publishing industry, but the situation in the publishing industry is like this. Some people say that the intellectual class has reached the end of the road this year. Although this is not entirely true, it is probably not far off.

Yearning for Foreign Lands 195

— Xi Jun

September dreams are light, as light as leaves falling from branches, bearing no weight. It is the most suitable season for missing someone! Although the grass and flowers in front of me have quietly withered by the low fence, faintly bearing the resentment of fading away; the white chrysanthemums are gradually blooming, facing the warm sunlight.

A kind of misty melancholy, like light smoke, climbs into my heart, and then climbs past it. As a result, I don't know why, but some regretful emotions arise. It's as if something is secretly holding me back. Therefore, my heart, my thoughts, have left this place, and like a pair of soaring swallows, fly over layers of mountains and layers of seas, to that distant, bright, ideal horizon. Although my body is bound by the present situation and has to stay here, my whole soul can be intoxicated in the dreamland of foreign lands day and night. Even if the scenery here can linger a little longer in my mind, giving me a little more warm and intimate feeling, it is still the last time. Yes, it's not that everything here is completely devoid of places that make me miss it. For this clear blue sky in September, the charming seasonal dreams, the bunches of late-ripening blood-red purple grapes overlapping on the rattan frame, smilingly adorable, and having whispered with a woman I admired among the grapevines, shoulder to shoulder, counting the stars in the sky together, humming the sweet Remona melody.

However, this period of soft life is rapidly passing away. Just like every flower, it bloomed and then withered. Moreover, when the autumn wind is already freezing into icicles in the northern country, will there still be pink shadows appearing from the snow? So I remained silent, simply discarding those past events. No nostalgia, no sighs, no tears, I plucked all the things that had taken root in my heart with all my might, threw them behind my head, and never looked back. I have already embraced new yearnings, replacing everything of the past.

I yearn for wandering in a foreign country, and I especially yearn for the elegant, beautiful, and affectionate waitresses in the cafes, following every stranger as eagerly as if they had met a long-lost lover. Every foreigner likes to immerse themselves in these places, and the lonely heart of a traveler will also feel comforted by this. To appreciate the taste of foreign customs!

The desire to appreciate the customs of the distant island on the other side has become an acute appetite disorder of the spirit recently, and I wish I could immediately grow wings under my arms and fly over there. Each day I can't go increases the weight of my worries, and this weight may increase to the point of crushing my body.

When will my fantasies bear fruit, this yearning for foreign lands!

An Analysis of Europeanized Vocabulary in Written Chinese (Part Two) 196

— Wang Fuquan

Similarly, it is very common to use European languages for units of measurement, with Chinese added above and below, such as "一(磅)朱奶" (one (pound) Zhunai [brand name of milk]), "一(听)(香烟)" (one (tin) (cigarettes)), etc. There is also a type of specialized term that becomes a "Chinese + European + Chinese" form, such as "(新)(罗曼)(主义)" ((New)(Romantic)(ism)), "(社会主义)(苏维埃)(共和国联盟)" ((Socialist)(Soviet)(Republic Union)) (Soviet originally meant council or committee), "(三)(A)(政策)" ((Three)(A)(Policy)), "(三)(B)(政策)" ((Three)(B)(Policy)), "(三)(C)(政策)" ((Three)(C)(Policy)), "(三)(K)(党)" ((Three)(K)(Party)), etc.

Several suffixes can also be pointed out.

-ize, -eify (化 -hua) | Idealize, scientize, commercialize, commoditize, automatize, literaryize, Europeanize

-ism (主义 zhuyi, 论 lun, 说 shuo, 制 zhi, 教 jiao) | Syndicalism, capitalism, the Three Principles of the People, naturalism; monism, pluralism, idealism, materialism, atomism, positivism; anthropocentrism, geocentrism, the doctrine of the creation of the soul, intellectualism, emotionalism, voluntarism; clan communism, promiscuity, monometallism, bimetallism, mixed gold-silver standard. Some are translated as "教" (jiao, religion), such as "拜物教" (baiwujiao, fetishism) (or translated as "灵物崇拜" (lingwu chongbai, spirit worship)).

-ty (性 xing) | Causality, generality, necessity, reality.

self (本身 benshen) | This thing itself, the text itself, science itself, he himself (or himself).

-tic (的 de) | Objective, active, absolute, leisurely, literary. "tic" is sometimes transliterated, such as "罗曼谛克" (luomandike, romantic).

In addition, such as "logy" being translated as "学" (xue, study), even our sages' classics have been Europeanized into "经学" (jingxue, classical studies). (There is also a very commonly used word "被" (bei, passive marker), such as "被选举权" (beixuanjuquan, right to be elected), "被压迫民族" (beiyapo minzu, oppressed nations), "被支配阶级" (beizhipei jieji, dominated class). This may have come from Japan.)

There are also quite a few prefixes.

anti- (反 fan) | Anti-revolution, anti-imperialist alliance, anti-Semitism.

Pan- (泛 fan) | Panpsychism, pansophy, Pan-European Union, Pan-Slavism, Pan-Pacific Science Conference.

un-, non- (不 bu, 非 fei) | Non-exhaustive, recession, unnatural; non-war, non-militarism.

Quasi- (准 zhun) | Quasi-national, quasi-criminal.

super- (超 chao) | Superman, super-economic exploitation, supraorganism, supernatural, supermoralism.

New- (新 xin) | New culture, Neo-Romanticism, Neo-Realism, New Economic Policy, Neo-Kantianism, new record, (New) economics (this "new" is a special usage from a technical point of view, but this type of usage is also very common).

The research on morphology is not very complicated and I also plan to write a little about it; as for syntax and rhetoric, it is not something that can be written down in a short time. As for the analysis of content, this is an even more arduous task and will have to wait until there is some progress in the history of various academic disciplines before starting.

Nature 197

— Kong Gong

People over the age of twenty gradually become thick-skinned and deep-hearted, unable to discern truth, falsehood, good, or evil. It is in old age, in childhood, or by chance that one can see the original face of humanity. This is what is called nature.

The Confucian division of pre-heaven and post-heaven is a wonderful interpretation. For thousands of years, mankind has desperately sought the so-called human nature, the original face of man, and finally, there has been no more perfect answer. But putting aside good and evil, the division between pre-heaven and post-heaven can explain many things. And human actions have not yet exceeded this range.

Just look at soldiers killing people, humans even eating human flesh during famines. What is different from children torturing insects, killing a bird, or killing a frog? The thought of sin is there at first, but it soon becomes natural (habit becomes second nature), because this is innate. It is not that there are so-called seeds of sin innately, but that the inherent nature of human beings, who have evolved to the present, is like this. So-called life and death are trivial matters.

However, mankind has stubbornly (evolved), and in fact, on the other hand, hasn't it degenerated, declined, established many names for the distinction between good and evil, for the standard of who should and should not survive? Therefore, the world is in turmoil, right and wrong are turned upside down, good people die early, and evil people prosper. Mankind constantly remakes weights and measures, but as a result, it has never measured the length or shortness of nature by an inch.

Hong Kong Foot (Part 1) 199

— Yu Shixia

(1)

(Treat the head when it hurts, treat the foot when it hurts.)

This saying is probably not only popular in Hunan. It doesn't consider the overall connection of things, only deals with them piecemeal; it doesn't solve them from the root, only handles the minor details. It's really a bit like "Treat the head when it hurts, treat the foot when it hurts!"

Headaches have always been my old problem. I remember when I was twelve or thirteen years old, I was studying at a normal school and suffered from malaria one summer. I was sick for more than two years in a row. Malaria is called "da baizi" (getting the shakes) in Hunan, and it is said that it is caused by "baizi" ghosts. At first, my "baizi" came every other day, then every two or three days, and then every ten or so days. Finally, it came on cloudy days and when it was windy and rainy, without a fixed date. When the "baizi" came, I always felt cold and shivering, my whole body trembling, and even covering myself with two or three quilts couldn't stop the cold. After the cold passed, I would have a fever, and my head would be dizzy and my eyes would blur, which was really uncomfortable. Usually, when the "baizi" didn't come, my head also felt heavy, and sometimes it felt very empty, and my feet had no strength, so I rarely went out. I was so weak and sickly that my classmates thought I was going to die young. Who knew that I haven't died yet, and several of those who were afraid that I would die young have already died!

For more than ten years, because the overall collapse of the rural economy has become more profound, my family's situation as a small landlord can no longer maintain the same state of well-being as before. Although I have never dreamed of inheriting a large fortune, I am also ashamed that I have no ability to reverse the family's misfortune under the general trend of economic bankruptcy. In addition, I got married and had children, and the burden became heavier day by day, and all kinds of worries came upon me. Fortunately, my body has become stronger day by day, not as thin as before, and my head no longer hurts. Although I have suffered from stomach problems for several years in these more than ten years, and I also had a dangerous appendicitis inflammation last year, my body gradually recovered after the illness. It seems that the Creator deliberately teased me, telling my body to be a little stronger so that I could bear this heavy burden of a miserable life. How can I put down this heavy burden?

My head no longer hurts, but my feet often itch and ache, and I didn't regard this rotten foot as a disease, but thought it was "Hunan foot," which Hunan people can't avoid.

Mr. Village Head (7) 200

— Wang Renshu

(That way, that way...)

Finally, trembling, one of them spoke inside.

"So what are your plans? I have to report to the superiors." The village head parted his knees, calmly, but furrowed his brow and said.

"Exempt, exempt, exempt from... can it be exempt?" These words were like timid mice, only sticking their heads out of the hole. Using the greatest courage, they only chewed out that half a sentence.

"How to exempt? How to exempt?" The village head shouted angrily. "You country bumpkins are really unreasonable. It wasn't me who told you to go. This is an order from above! For you, I have really worn out the soles of my feet, and spoken until my teeth bleed. But the district chief always blames me!

"No way! No way! No matter what! The first batch must be fifty! Fifty! Fifty! There are five of you in the three villages above and below, isn't five a lot?"

"The district chief is still forcing me to hand over people today. I have no way, so I tricked him. (Wait until tomorrow! Wait until tomorrow!) But tomorrow will pass! Damn it! What an unlucky year! I don't want to do this lousy job anymore..."

"That won't work! You still have to be the village head." Pretending to laugh. They must flatter the superiors, that is their philosophy of life.

Geneva Chinese Painting Exhibition 204

More than 46,000 Visitors

Rolland Romain Extols Vigorously

Since our government dispatched Liu Haisu to Germany last year to exhibit Chinese paintings and promote Eastern art, grand Chinese painting exhibitions have been held successively in Berlin, Hamburg, cities along the Rhine River, as well as Amsterdam and The Hague in the Netherlands, all of which have garnered great acclaim. This summer, upon the invitation of the Swiss government and the Geneva municipal government, Liu once again brought his entire collection of 280 works to Geneva for a public exhibition lasting one month. We have now received a letter from Geneva detailing the situation of this exhibition, and we present a summary below. Geneva is a world-famous city, the center of international politics and a cultural hub. The Chinese painting exhibition was held in the Municipal Historical Art Museum, a magnificent stone structure with exquisite carvings, spanning hundreds of feet in the center of Geneva. The entrance is solemn and several feet high, with a park outside. The interior lighting is suitable, and our country's famous works are displayed within, complementing each other perfectly. July 19th was the official opening day of the Chinese painting exhibition. Prior to this, the municipal government widely distributed invitations, inviting celebrities and scholars from various countries residing in Geneva. At this time, the International Cultural Conference was being held in Geneva, so dignitaries from various countries gathered there. Former French Prime Minister Édouard Herriot and literary giant Romain Rolland also attended the event. Rolland praised it incessantly, saying, "Chinese painters, after a process of soulful brewing and disciplined synthesis of various natural impressions, re-express a new, complete, and ideal world. This is true art." Rolland is a great literary figure of our time, wielding authority in the modern ideological world, and his comments are conclusive. A certain Japanese representative to the International Cultural Conference stated that the splendor and magnificence of modern Chinese painting are unmatched by Japanese painters. The great critic Hugger, in a review published in the Geneva News, said, "Chinese painting techniques have a completely different starting point from European art, but among the millions of viewers, there is unanimous sympathy and praise for this Chinese painting exhibition, and they can understand it thoroughly without confusion. It can be seen that the transcendental ideals of the East are gradually being accepted and absorbed by Westerners. We Westerners have been bound by material things for too long. Chinese art respects individuality, respects the self, and applies the spirit of the self to objective materials. For example, painting the flowers of the four seasons, or the Three Friends of Winter (pine, bamboo, and plum), is never tiresome and is handled in a cyclical manner, achieving a profound effect with its constantly vivid rhythms." He added, "I predict that this Chinese painting exhibition will have a tremendous impact on the European art scene."

After Mr. and Mrs. Liu Haisu arrived in Geneva, they were welcomed by the audience every time they attended the event. Many painters asked Liu to purchase Chinese paper, brushes, ink, and colors. An elderly painter over seventy years old, Bcrun, tightly grasped Liu's hand in the crowd, insisted on seeing Liu's painting of a large pine, and asked for paper and ink, saying, "Seeing Chinese painting has solved my decades of torment. For decades, I have been a mere imitator of nature, simply depicting a semblance of the natural world. Now, my artistic demands lie elsewhere." The Chinese painting exhibition in Geneva lasted for one month, with a total of more than 46,000 visitors. More than 200 artists were represented. It is reported that the exhibition will move to Bern, the capital of Switzerland, on August 25th.

Educational Situation in Various Counties of Zhejiang Province Nearing Stagnation 205

Direct Shortfall of Over One Million Yuan in Funding

Nearly 20,000 Teachers and Staff Will Lose Their Jobs

The Number of Children and Adults Out of School Will Increase by 400,000

The sources of local education funding in various counties of Zhejiang Province are mainly land tax surcharges, land rent, and local taxes. Over the years, due to repeated disasters and poor harvests, rural areas have gone bankrupt, and land tax collection has fallen short, to the extent that the funds of various counties have been almost exhausted, and most counties are in debt by several thousand to tens of thousands of yuan. The situation in various counties was already extremely difficult this year. In recent months, some local taxes were deemed excessively burdensome and were abolished by the provincial government, which was announced in early August. The provincial government will find other ways to compensate for the loss, but subsidies will only be available from October. August and September have already been announced as abolished, and collection is impossible. These funds have already been greatly affected. Now, after a severe drought, disaster areas are spread throughout the province. Although the busy season for land tax collection has been extended to February, many counties have collected less than 10% of the amount. With the regular tax insufficient, the surcharge will naturally fall short as well. As for land rent, there is even less rent to collect. It is estimated that the annual expenditure budget for education funding in various counties and cities of Zhejiang Province is approximately 3.3 million yuan, excluding district funds and private school expenses. There are approximately 12,000 elementary schools, 2,400 people's schools, 31,000 elementary school teachers and staff, 6,000 people's school teachers and staff, 710,000 elementary school students, and 100,000 people's school students. Furthermore, of the 3.3 million yuan in education funding from various counties, approximately 1.98 million yuan comes from land tax and 250,000 yuan from school land rent, accounting for approximately two-thirds of the total education funding in various counties, all of which are directly affected by the disaster. Even if the income for this year is calculated at an average of 50%, there will still be a shortfall of over 1.1 million yuan. The impact of other miscellaneous tax reductions and exemptions, as well as district funds and private schools, is not included in this figure. Based on the current situation, if even half of the elementary and people's schools in various counties are forced to close, nearly 20,000 elementary and people's school teachers and staff will lose their jobs, and over 350,000 elementary school students and over 50,000 adults will be out of school. The crisis is intensifying, and if no appropriate solution is found, the future is unimaginable.
