Municipal Bureau of Education Schedules Holiday Homework Exhibition 211

Starting October 20th at Wanzhu Elementary School

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education has issued instructions to the principals of all elementary schools, stating that the bureau has already instructed schools to prepare for the exhibition of holiday homework of elementary school children. The scope of exhibits for the exhibition will be divided into the following three categories:

Scope of Exhibits 212

A. Competition materials for elementary school subjects stipulated by the Children's Morning Newspaper, as announced in the Bureau's Education Weekly Issues 24 and 27. B. Materials created by children from various schools during this summer vacation. C. Holiday homework materials determined by the schools themselves during this summer vacation. In order to facilitate the selection of children's works by various schools and to give children ample opportunity for observation, the Bureau has specially formulated nine articles on the preparatory exhibition methods for holiday homework of various elementary schools, which are attached to the instructions. Each school should hold a preliminary exhibition of the holiday homework results of children in grades 3 and above on any Sunday before the date of the Holiday Homework Exhibition Conference convened by the Bureau, and then select excellent works according to the stipulated standards and send them to the conference for display. What each school must pay attention to is that this kind of results exhibition is to examine the true situation of children's holiday homework, so that it can be used as a mirror to promote children's extracurricular activities in the future and to seek a practical connection between family and school. Therefore, the exhibits should be absolutely authentic and should never be false. The conference has been scheduled to be held at the Municipal Wanzhu Elementary School from October 20th. All municipal and registered private elementary schools should send exhibits to the conference on time for display. This order is for compliance and implementation.

Preparatory Exhibition 213

Methods for the Preparatory Exhibition of Holiday Homework Results of Elementary Schools: (1) All municipal and registered private elementary schools in the city should hold a preparatory exhibition before officially participating in the Bureau's Holiday Homework Results Exhibition to give children ample opportunity for observation and to prepare for formal participation. (2) The exhibits for the preparatory exhibition are limited to those created during this summer vacation in each school. (3) The scope of exhibits for the preparatory exhibition includes the competition materials stipulated by the Children's Morning Newspaper announced in the Bureau's Education Weekly Issues 247, the holiday homework materials determined by each school itself this summer, and the materials created by children during the summer vacation. (4) The preparatory exhibition will be held on any Sunday before the official opening of the conference and will invite children's parents to attend and visit to achieve the effect of connecting family and school education. (5) The criticism of the preparatory exhibition will be the responsibility of the teachers and staff of each school. (6) The awards for the preparatory exhibition will be determined by each school itself. (7) All children in grades 3 and above must participate in the preparatory exhibition (children who are physically weak or have serious physical and mental defects, and children who have entered health camps this summer may be exempted from participation). (8) After the preparatory exhibition is over, the better exhibits should be marked in each grade and at least one-tenth of them should be kept in the school, which will be used as exhibits to participate in the Bureau's Holiday Homework Results Exhibition. (9) The situation of the preparatory exhibition should be reported to the Bureau at any time for reference.

New Work in the Fanwangdu Universal Education Experiment Zone 216

The Fanwangdu Universal Education Experiment Zone in this port is jointly operated by Datong University and the Huxi Nian'ershe. The goal of the experiment is to implement people's livelihood-oriented education, with saving the nation and preventing its demise as the backbone, advocating the use of domestic goods, promoting social frugality, striving for social production, developing the rural economy, improving the lives of the people, and jointly planning the rejuvenation of the Chinese nation. The experimental method is to take the entire area as a whole educational place, cancel the school form, and all education starts from the economy. The methods of class starting and dismissal, winter and summer vacations, semesters, and academic years are abolished. In order to implement this ideal, the area specially invited Mr. Shuangqiu to create a universal education vehicle. Mr. began to study and experiment with it last fall, and completed one this spring. It is shaped like a wooden box, about two feet long and high, and about one foot wide. A blackboard is set up on the top, and the upper layer is divided into several compartments to place samples of agricultural products and seeds for exhibition at any time. The lower layer is also divided into several compartments, which can be used to place educational supplies and health supplies. There is also a movable wooden frame on the vehicle, which can hang several kinds of popular readings. There are four wheels underneath, which can be pushed to various places, or sent to the education department, or sent to the field for education. It has all the functions of a classroom, a mobile library, and a mobile exhibition. Mr. Tai has recently realized that education funding is the foundation for promoting universal education, and in order to expand the effectiveness of the vehicle, he has reproduced a larger universal education vehicle, which is about twice the size of the previous one, and has the functions of a classroom, exhibition hall, mobile book vehicle, mobile bookstore, and bedding, etc. The vehicle is also equipped with a movable cloth curtain, which can cover more than a dozen people when it is opened, and takes up very little space when folded and placed on the vehicle. There are also seven movable benches inside, which can seat fourteen people, which is especially convenient when teaching. The purpose of this vehicle is to promote domestic goods, relieve youth, improve rural areas, and popularize education. According to the person in charge of the area, starting this fall, they plan to recruit several young people with junior high school education as universal education service personnel to promote domestic goods and promote education at the same time. The living expenses of the personnel will be taken from the commission earned from promoting domestic goods. The detailed methods have been formulated and will be implemented soon.

British Team Wins First Race in Anglo-American Yacht Race

(Havas News Agency, Newport, Rhode Island, USA, 17th) In the Anglo-American yacht race for the America's Cup, which has historically been held by the United States, the British yacht "Endeavour" won the first race this year. The entire course was thirty miles. "Endeavour" finished in three hours, forty-three minutes, and forty-four seconds (the previous record was three hours, twenty-five minutes, and twenty-nine seconds, set in 1893), two minutes and eleven seconds faster than the American "Rainbow". President Roosevelt also watched the race from here.

Chronicles of Xiaoxitian Spring and Autumn by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Acting as a Merchant Enters the Folk Road, Returns to Yongshou, Bids Farewell, a Heavenly Person Arrives in Chang'an

Cheng Zhi felt that this person was tactless and became sullen, looking up at the mausoleum. Only then did Zhang Jiefu stop talking. This mausoleum was about five or six zhang high and seven or eight zhang long, resembling a small mound. Because the front of the mausoleum was the back of the main hall, there was no open space for maneuvering. A tall stele stood in front of the mausoleum, boldly inscribed "Tomb of King Wen of Zhou." Behind this mausoleum, about forty or fifty zhang away, was another mausoleum, accessible via a stone pine path. A dozen or so small steles lined both sides of the path, serving as minimal decorations. In front of the mausoleum was also a large stele, inscribed "Tomb of King Wu of Zhou." The open space around the mausoleum was vast and empty, with only some Chinese toon saplings planted. There were two types of Chinese toon: one was fragrant toon, whose buds could be eaten as vegetables, and the other was stinky toon, whose branches were extremely fragile and easily broken, exuding an unpleasant odor in the sap—these were the ones planted here. These toon saplings were less than two chi tall, with finger-thick trunks protruding from the weeds, spaced four or five steps apart, swaying forlornly in the wind. Even in Cheng Zhi's eyes, the place seemed exceedingly desolate. This was after the director and ministers had visited and ordered renovations. Had one come here before the renovations, they would likely have seen only two overgrown, weedy mounds. Seeing their silence, Director Chang asked with a smile, "Mr. Cheng, what are your impressions after visiting this place?" Cheng Zhiqian replied, "I think most people who come to visit the Northwest feel similarly—that it's cold and harsh. I also believe that the scenic spots here shouldn't be too extravagant. Excessive extravagance would make people think, 'Living people don't have enough to eat, so why is there money to decorate the tombs of the dead?'" Director Chang clapped his hands twice, saying, "Excellent, excellent! If everyone who comes to the Northwest had this perspective, we would welcome them wholeheartedly."

(Papa) (Mama)

Recently, Japanese Minister of Education Matsuda banned children in elementary schools and kindergartens nationwide from using the terms "(Papa)" and "(Mama)," claiming they harm Japanese customs. What are the traditional Japanese customs? Matsuda didn't say. How much harm do Japanese children using "(Papa)" and "(Mama)" cause to Japanese customs? He also didn't say. If "(Papa)" and "(Mama)" are banned, what terms does Matsuda plan to replace them with? He didn't say either. Although this is a trivial issue that seems to carry a hint of "effeminacy," because Matsuda is Japan's Minister of Education and we see his opinions published in the newspapers as so "refined," it makes one feel a noteworthy interest.

In China, if children speak Mandarin, they mostly call their fathers "(Papa)" and their mothers "(Mama)." This terminology has a long history and is very common. But in Japan, Matsuda says they harm the country's customs. What does he mean? It's impossible to guess. If it's because Chinese children are shouting "(Papa)" and "(Mama)," and it's believed that Japanese children are influenced by China, hindering the country's customs, then if this assumption is correct, Matsuda's "Yamato" spirit is worthy of admiration!

In China, what we see and hear are indeed many Western terms! And it cannot be said that there are few Eastern terms either. But the Chinese use "promotion" instead of "prohibition," so Chinese customs are always so bad, so bad that even "(Papa)" and "(Mama)" are banished to the cold palace! (?)

Here, I have another thought.

In Shanghai, "(Papa)" and "(Mama)," especially "(Mama)," call their own children "(Younger Brother)" and "(Younger Sister)," abandoning the former style of "(Sweetheart)" and "(Treasure)"; who started this? What does it mean? It's unfathomable! I think Matsuda rarely hears this kind of "(neither fish nor fowl)" terminology! If Japanese "(Papa)" and "(Mama)" must be banished to the cold palace, what should be done with Shanghai's "(Younger Brother)" and "(Younger Sister)"? Should this unique Chinese "innovation" be encouraged and promoted? I hope our "(Minister of Education)" can publish some insights!

Casual Chat on Eyebrow Painting by Qifenglou Lord

Loving beauty is human nature, especially for women. Modern women today compete in adornment. Besides clothing, they also engage in beautifying their faces, blending powder and rouge, gently applying and smoothing, admiring their reflections in the mirror countless times. Adding eyebrow painting is considered an important task, as slender crescent brows arched into the temples indeed possess unique charm. However, in the past, women mostly lightly applied kohl to their eyebrows or simply burned willow branches to add a touch of color. Nowadays, so-called socialites and beauties have escalated the practice, creating new styles. They shave off their natural eyebrows entirely and freely apply imported eyebrow cream to repaint them. Nothing could be more contradictory! Is it an attempt to change one's heart by first changing one's face? Occasionally, when I talk to them, they retort, "Have you not heard of Zhang Jingzhao painting eyebrows? The ancients created it, and we, the descendants, follow it. It doesn't seem excessive, so why criticize us so harshly!" I silently withdraw, pondering the legacy of Jingzhao.

According to records, Zhang Jingzhao, named Chang, a descendant of later generations, once served as the magistrate of Jingzhao, hence the name. He once painted eyebrows for his wife, which later generations admired and considered a romantic affair. However, I heard from an elder that "Jingzhao's eyebrow painting was not solely for enhancing his wife's beauty. There was another love story behind it, one filled with tender and poignant emotions. It is said that Chang, in his childhood, was handsome and charming. One night, he dreamed of an old man with a white beard who, upon being asked about his ideal partner, pointed to a girl in a straw pile in the tofu shop next door, saying, 'This is your wife.' The next day, he went to see her. The girl was crying, dirty, with tears and snot streaming down her face. Chang, young and impetuous, was furious at the sight! He picked up a stone and threw it at the girl's face, intending to flee, thinking he would find a better match. As a result, the girl only had a break in her left eyebrow, and fortunately, she was unharmed. Later, the girl grew up and was adopted by a gentleman as his adopted daughter. At this time, Chang had also become an official and had a good reputation, which the gentleman heard of. Learning that he was unmarried, he married his adopted daughter to Chang. On the wedding night, the candlelight illuminated her red makeup, revealing her graceful figure. However, there was a break in her eyebrows. When asked about it, the girl told him about the incident from years ago. Chang was filled with shame and guilt! He quickly picked up a brush and painted a continuation to cover the mark," and so on.

In summary, Chang painted eyebrows for his wife to cover a scar. Compared to modern women's artificiality, the intentions are vastly different.

A Fragrant Cloud of Eastern Incense by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

After they finished playing the Marseillaise, she specifically instructed Li Lianying to personally retrieve all the instruments, one by one, so she could examine them repeatedly. At the same time, she had them perch side by side on a beautifully designed branch. At each end of the branch, there was a small white jade cup filled with water and food for them to eat and drink. Upon seeing this special gift, the Empress Dowager seemed extremely pleased. She even thought she couldn't see clearly enough, so she instructed Li Lianying to bring it closer, about two or three feet away from her, so she could examine it carefully. At that time, we couldn't help but laugh secretly, thinking that these two parrots were just ordinary birds and didn't deserve the Empress Dowager's attention, treating them with such seriousness! Unexpectedly, after two or three minutes, they immediately showed their special talents, surprising everyone. One of the two parrots suddenly cried out in a clear voice, "Long live the Empress Dowager!" This cry completely astonished everyone! Especially because its pronunciation was so accurate, it sounded exactly like a child speaking, which made people even more astonished. Just as everyone was whispering and marveling, the other parrot suddenly shouted, "Peace to the Empress Dowager!"

I think Yuan Shikai must have put a lot of effort into making these two birds speak such clear phrases. At the very least, he must have had someone who was skilled at raising birds teach them for him. Otherwise, even if they could speak, they wouldn't be able to say it so perfectly at the right time.

The Physiognomy of Shuang Yu's Painting and Calligraphy by Yin

Mr. Tang Dingzhi, a descendant of Qin Yin, recently adopted the alias Shuang Yu Daoren. Anyone who knows Dingzhi should understand the meaning behind it. There are many examples of using aliases to depict the past and present, but none are as humorous as these two characters. Daoren's paintings excel in their unconstrained style, particularly his large-scale works. Last year, he created twelve eight-foot screens for a certain gentleman, which were admired by all who saw them. This is because Daoren entered painting through calligraphy, and his calligraphy is like a celestial horse soaring through the sky, unbound. I remember when Daoren traveled in Guangdong and Guangxi, he enjoyed composing poems. Friends once praised him for his mastery of painting, calligraphy, and poetry. Since the Restoration, he has stopped discussing poetry and devoted himself to physiognomy, which he highly values. He even ranks physiognomy, calligraphy, and painting as his three excellences. This is probably Tang Jun's self-deprecation, meant ironically.

Small Recipe: Local Mooncakes and Cantonese Mooncakes by Zhang Huang

The Chinese people are most unwilling to easily let go of their culinary pleasures. Whenever major or minor festivals arrive, every household, big and small, always prepares one or several customary foods that are considered essential for the occasion, ostensibly as a formality, but in reality, it is for the sake of the public's palate.

During the Mid-Autumn Festival, the most luminous and spherical moon in nature is at its prime, so the symbolic mooncakes also occupy a prominent position among the timely foods. Are these foods particularly unique or independent in taste or crafting techniques? They use the same ingredients as ordinary cakes, dumplings, and buns, making dough for the skin and filling it with sweet or savory ingredients. If the filling is more precious, the taste will be more palatable.

Jiangnan, the prosperous land of abundance, produces exquisite products renowned throughout the country. Moreover, the meticulous Suzhou people, known for their delicate snacks (tea cakes), earn some respect for the Zhejiang people. However, on such a major holiday, the timely mooncakes, whether sold in stores or made privately (in fact, very few people make mooncakes themselves), are not particularly outstanding in taste. The most frustrating experience occurred in my childhood when an elder gave me a box of four Suzhou-style sweet mooncakes. The box was made of wooden slats, wrapped in white paper, with a red paper label pasted on the front, looking neat and presentable. This was the elder's customary holiday gift, supposedly catering to my fondness for sweets. Feeling grateful, I excitedly opened the box to eat. The piece of inedible paper stuck to the bottom of the mooncake was painstakingly removed, making me slightly annoyed. Unexpectedly, the half-mooncake I bit into had a thick, burnt, and greasy skin, filled with hardened lumps of cheap sugar, so-called "too sweet to eat, too bad to waste." Ultimately, I couldn't bear the sweetness and secretly went out to vomit. Since then, I have completely lost interest in eating mooncakes during the Mid-Autumn Festival!

Cantonese-style mooncakes are quite different. The size of the cakes varies, but the skin is always soft and glutinous. Unless they have been stored for too long, they also have a hint of sweetness, which is a significant advantage. The fillings also come in many varieties, all made with careful preparation and considered well-matched. In recent years, Cantonese mooncakes have been promoted almost nationwide and have successfully invaded the mooncake market in the Jiangzhe region, occupying a large portion of the local products' market share. This shows that even with leisure foods, which seem trivial, one must still research and seek improvement. If one remains stuck in the old methods of centuries ago, superior products will naturally rise to replace them. Like local mooncakes, even if they are not squeezed to the point of being lost, they will likely disappoint the festival and be lamented by connoisseurs!

Cantonese mooncake shops, like other mooncake shops, begin production and sales from the beginning of the seventh lunar month. Each shop utilizes its expertise to innovate and introduce new products, bestowing auspicious names and even creating special price lists, treating it as a serious matter. With shared tastes, the shops with better products are often swamped with customers. For example, the three major companies in Shanghai temporarily suspend the production of Western pastries to focus all their efforts on making Cantonese mooncakes. This period of business is undoubtedly dedicated to providing food. But why do all the shops in the city stop selling Cantonese mooncakes as soon as the Mid-Autumn Festival is over? I think the many gourmets in the city certainly won't act in unison and stop eating Cantonese mooncakes because they are out of season. I wonder if there is any special reason for this. I'll have to ask Mr. Xi, the owner of Guanshengyuan, when I see him.

Letter to the Editor: In the Women's Special Issue on September 1st ("A Visit to the Former Residence of Concubine Ming"), the plaque was written by Hua Shikui, not Yan Xiu. The address is east of the Drum Tower, not north of the Drum Tower. Mr. Shajin passed by hastily at dusk, so the above errors are unavoidable. Please correct them to ensure accuracy. Also, Tan Lane is now called Feijia Hutong. The descendants of the Fei family still reside nearby, but many are scattered. From Tianjin, Anonymous.

Commercial News: Financial and Gold Markets Still Oppressed by Foreign Exchange

Continued decline of 6.9 yuan, breaking the 40-yuan mark

The gold market, with few short positions and a relatively stable front, but under the pressure of loose and excessive supply, continued to fall due to hedging sales. Initially, the overseas silver market saw a rise in both London and New York, and there was talk of the United States tending to buy after the close, which dampened market sentiment. Banks' selling intention is unabated

According to foreign telegrams yesterday, London large bars, both near and far, rose by 0.0625. After opening, the banks had a slight appetite for selling, and HSBC Bank announced the listing of British and American, both rising by 125, but the overall situation was still hovering. In the morning, the banks' selling intention was very eager, and the gold market also trended downstream, with the process becoming more hardened. Financial Outlook: Seemingly Quiet

Interbank lending rate slightly fell, clearing houses still operating

Although the financial background seems extraordinarily exhausted, as seen in the Bund mortgage crisis a few days ago, even harsh conditions were being refused. Fortunately, there are many individuals in the financial sector who are dedicated to public service and understand that without mutual solidarity, the financial system will inevitably collapse. Therefore, on one hand, they are joining hands, and on the other hand, they are trying their best to lower the interbank lending rate to calm the market. Yesterday, the market even fell by two cents. Both the early and noon markets were at 1.3 cents, while the clearing house rate remained at 2 cents, not speculating even as the Mid-Autumn Festival approached. This is a good sign for our financial sector and is also something readers will be happy to hear. Discounted bill transactions: Over 3.9 million in early market transfers and new transactions, over 400,000 in noon market transactions, over 300,000 in small general association transactions, over 900,000 in foreign mortgage transactions, and over 1.5 million in new deals. Youth Association Reading Group Seeking New Members 222

The Shanghai Youth Association, in order to encourage young people's interest in reading and cultivate their ability to explore issues, has organized several reading groups. Chinese Walking Association Schedules Public Walking Competition 227

Finish Line Changed to Shen Garden

In order to promote and popularize walking skills, the Chinese Walking Association, in addition to participating in the annual International Walking Competition, has launched the Shanghai Open Walking Competition for men and women. With the assistance of the Sports Advancement Association since the 20th year, it has been held annually for four sessions. This year's competition, after being decided by the association's committee in April, is scheduled to be held on November 4th. The men's race is 13 miles, and the women's race has been increased to two miles. The finish line was originally set at the Chinese Athletics Field on Route Père Robert, but now that the field has been converted into a hospital and the Sports Association has moved to Shen Garden on Yanping Road, the route has also been changed accordingly (see route below). The entire route is thirteen and one-third miles long. The women's race will be held inside the athletics field, running eight laps around the track, a total of 3,200 meters. Training will begin soon. Those who are unfamiliar with the correct posture can join the training class at the association's location at the Moore Memorial Church on Xizang Road. Women can write to the association to request guidance. It is reported that the association will start accepting registrations next month (October). The route is as follows: starting from the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Tongfu Road, via Great Western Road, Brennan Road, turning into Warren Road, Hongqiao Road, straight into Yaoyan Jiao Road, Avenue Petain, Avenue Joffre, Avenue du Roi Albert, Seymour Road, to Xinzha Road, passing Ba Xia Sha Du Road, Connaught Road, Yanping Road, and ending inside the Shen Garden Athletics Field.

Furthermore, it is reported that the association has scheduled a 17-mile walking practice this Sunday (the 23rd) at 7:00 AM. Those who wish to join must first register with the association and gather at the intersection of Tongfu Road on that day, departing on time. It is heard that the veteran 石金生 (Shi Jinsheng), who retired last year, has regained his momentum this year and is training with 周余愚 (Zhou Yuyu) and others for the 50,000-meter race. It can be predicted that he will achieve excellent results in the future.
